<teammate-message teammate_id="jhin" color="pink" summary="All three PR reviews complete — findings summary">
All three reviews posted as `gh pr comment`. Summary:

**PR #147 (A1 skeleton) — LGTM, no blockers.** `it.todo` is correct when Vitest isn't installed yet. Minor observation: jhin session files from commit `420331c` appear in the diff but are already on main as untracked — no net change. Unblocks downstream tasks.

**PR #148 (I2 IAM) — LGTM with one IMPORTANT finding.** `roles/firebaseauth.admin` is over-privileged for the stated purpose of ID token verification. Firebase Admin SDK `verifyIdToken()` is a public-key operation and requires no IAM role at all — granting full Auth admin exposes user create/delete/update if the SA is ever compromised. Recommend removing the role. Storage bucket-scoping via `gsutil iam ch` is correct. One suggestion: use a bash array for the bucket list instead of unquoted string. Not a hard merge blocker for staging, but should be fixed before prod.

**PR #146 (J1 regression lane) — LGTM, no blockers.** xfail-flip discipline (`33948bf` → `680bafd`) is clean. PR template Testing section is well-structured and reusable. Minor: the `__dirname + ../../../` path anchor in the self-referential test would silently break if the file depth changes — not a blocker.

Comment URLs:
- #147: https://github.com/Duongntd/strawberry/pull/147#issuecomment-4273086902
- #148: https://github.com/Duongntd/strawberry/pull/148#issuecomment-4273087206
- #146: https://github.com/Duongntd/strawberry/pull/146#issuecomment-4273087446
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="caitlyn" color="blue" summary="ADR §9 firebaseauth.admin drift">
Viktor's #148 fix surfaced a real issue in the approved architecture plan.

**ADR §9** (`plans/approved/2026-04-17-test-dashboard-architecture.md`) lists `roles/firebaseauth.admin` as required for Cloud Run SA "to verify ID tokens via Admin SDK." **This is wrong.** `verifyIdToken()` uses Google's public JWKS endpoint — zero IAM needed. `firebaseauth.admin` would grant full user CRUD on SA compromise — a significant overprivilege.

Jhin caught it on #148 review; Viktor fixed the script (two bindings now: datastore.user + bucket-scoped storage.objectAdmin). But the ADR text still says three bindings including firebaseauth.admin.

**Follow-up chore recommended:** patch ADR §9 to remove the firebaseauth.admin line and clarify that ID token verification is JWKS-based. Cheap fix, prevents the next implementer reading the plan from re-introducing the overprivilege (my brief to Viktor did exactly that — I copied the three-binding list from the ADR verbatim).

Not a blocker — Viktor's script is authoritative. But the plan-as-source-of-truth is load-bearing for strawberry, and a wrong IAM claim in an approved plan is a security footgun waiting for the next session. Suggest one of Azir, Viktor, or me opens a small `chore:` patch PR against that section. Happy to draft it if you want it coming from me.

Unrelated note: board unchanged otherwise, still six PRs in dual-review.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="caitlyn" color="blue" summary="#152 uses feat: — rule 5 ambiguity for dashboards/">
Noticed on #152 (Seraphine, G1): PR uses `feat:` prefix. Others in the dashboards workstream use `chore:`.

**Rule 5 ambiguity surfacing:** CLAUDE.md rule 5 requires `feat:`/`fix:`/etc. for code commits touching `apps/**` (these feed release-please), and `chore:`/`ops:` for non-code. `dashboards/` is new — it's code, it's a new release-please package per A2 (tag `test-dashboard-v*`). So `feat:` is semantically correct for G1 (a new feature in the test-dashboard package). But the rule text doesn't explicitly cover `dashboards/**`.

Three ways this could go:
1. **`feat:` is correct** (my read) — dashboards/ is a new release-please watch path, feat/fix/perf/refactor apply. Rule 5 text needs a small amendment to include `dashboards/**` alongside `apps/**`. Seraphine got it right; others (Jayce, Vi, Ekko) used chore: out of caution.
2. **`chore:` is correct** — until A2 (#3, not yet done) actually lands release-please config, dashboards/ has no release-please track, so feat: is premature.
3. **Pre-push hook decides** — if it only checks apps/**, it lets both through silently. If it excludes dashboards/ from the feat: allowlist, #152 gets blocked.

Worth a human call from Duong on which way the rule should read before merges start. I can't check the hook behavior without running it, and pushing to find out would create noise.

**No implementer action needed from me right now** — Seraphine's PR is internally consistent and QA-note-acceptable. Flagging so rule 5 gets clarified before the merge wave starts and to avoid Jhin having to re-review if prefix needs changing.

## Duong — 2026-04-18T07:13:34Z

<teammate-message teammate_id="caitlyn" color="blue" summary="Two hygiene rules + critical xfail config defect">
Team-wide heads-up — two items from Evelynn/Azir review findings:

**1. Merge origin/main into your branch before pushing.**

#150 and #151 branches carried unrelated plan-file drift (delete of dependabot-remediation.md, add of p1-2-lib-sh-tdd.md) because their bases were stale. Catch it yourself before Jhin/Azir have to flag it:
```
git fetch origin && git merge origin/main
git diff origin/main --stat   # sanity-check only your intended files changed
```
Do this *before* pushing. Not after. Not rebasing — merge (rule 11).

**2. CRITICAL TDD DEFECT in Vitest config pattern — do NOT copy from #151.**

Azir found a load-bearing bug: both vitest configs in #151 include `exclude: ["**/*.xfail.test.ts"]`. This silently skips every xfail-marked file, which means:
- `tdd-gate.yml` parses test output and sees no xfail markers
- The xfail-first rule (CLAUDE.md #12) becomes a no-op
- Every PR on TDD-enabled packages passes the gate without actually proving xfail discipline

Vi is fixing on her branch. Until her fix lands, **do not copy #151's vitest config for other packages** (future dashboards sub-packages, new services). The right pattern is to INCLUDE `**/*.xfail.test.ts` in the test run — xfail tests are supposed to execute and record as expected-failures, not be skipped.

Impact for in-flight branches:
- Anyone who copied #151's vitest.config.ts pattern: stop, wait for Vi's fix, copy the corrected pattern.
- Anyone authoring xfail seeds: ensure your xfail files are actually executing in your local `pnpm test:unit` output before committing. If you don't see them in the test count, the config is excluding them.

Questions to me or Evelynn. Carry on.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="azir" color="red" summary="ADR amend blocked by pre-commit guard — need guidance">
Blocked on amending ADR §9. Need your guidance — will NOT bypass hooks.

**What happened.** Made the §9 edit (remove `firebaseauth.admin`, add rationale sentence) and staged only the plan file. My diff is exactly one replaced bullet — no secret introduced. Pre-commit secrets guard tripped on Guard 4 (scrub-and-detect):

```
BLOCK: plans/approved/2026-04-17-test-dashboard-architecture.md contains a string matching a known decrypted secret value
```

**Root cause.** The ADR has always contained `ALLOWED_UIDS=0DJzc86i5MP74jAwwT4YjvbcAub2` at §7 (line 326). That UID is also present in `secrets/encrypted/dashboards.*.age`. Guard 4 scans the *whole staged blob* against decrypted values and has no `plans/` allowlist (unlike Guards 1–3). So any edit to this ADR will re-trigger this block even though the literal was committed on 2026-04-17 in the original promotion and my diff doesn't touch it.

**Options (prefer your call):**
1. **Redact the UID from the ADR.** Replace `ALLOWED_UIDS=0DJzc...` with `ALLOWED_UIDS=<see secrets/encrypted/dashboards.*.env.age>`. This is arguably the right long-term fix — the UID isn't secret per se, but Guard 4 treats "anything also in plaintext of a .age blob" as a secret, and the ADR shouldn't carry values duplicated from encrypted env.
2. **Add `plans/` to Guard 4's allowlist in `scripts/hooks/pre-commit-secrets-guard.sh`.** Consistent with Guards 1–3 which already allowlist `plans/`. Cleaner but touches hook code — a scripts/ change, separate concern.
3. **Bypass with `--no-verify`** — NO. Rule 14 forbids; I'm not doing this.

I lean (1): it's minimal scope, correct defense-in-depth, and lets me land the §9 amend in the same commit. Which do you want? I have the edit ready to re-stage either way.

(Also note: three uncommitted files in the working tree belong to other agents — jhin memory/learnings, seraphine learnings — none mine. I staged only my ADR file, so they're untouched.)

## Evelynn — 2026-04-18T07:14:32Z

Three things blocked on you. Details:

---

**1. F4 encrypted env bundle — hard blocker for Phase 1 exit**

Task #19. Agents can't author it because strawberry rule 6 forbids agents from reading plaintext secrets. You generate the values, age-encrypt them, commit the `.age` ciphertext to `secrets/env/`.

What's needed:
- `INGEST_TOKEN` — 32-byte random, for reporter → dashboard POSTs. `openssl rand -hex 32` works.
- `FIREBASE_PROJECT_ID` — likely `myapps-b31ea` for prod, `myapps-b31ea-staging` for staging.
- `GCS_BUCKET` — `strawberry-test-artifacts-prod` / `-staging` (already provisioned by Viktor's B2).
- `ALLOWED_UIDS` — comma-sep list of Firebase UIDs (yours, Haruka's) permitted to view the dashboard.

Without this, Viktor can't finish I1 (deploy script) → no Cloud Run service → no H1/H2 reporter wiring → **Phase 1 exit ("unit test result visible at `/` within 5s") is unreachable.**

Procedure: `tools/decrypt.sh` has an encrypt mode, or use `tools/encrypt.sh` directly. Drop ciphertext into `secrets/env/prod.env.age` + `staging.env.age`. Commit with `ops:` prefix.

---

**2. Rule 5 clarification: does `dashboards/**` take `feat:` or `chore:`?**

CLAUDE.md rule 5 currently says: `apps/**` = `feat:/fix:/...` (feeds release-please), everything else = `chore:/ops:`. `dashboards/` is new; it's getting its own release-please track (A2 #3 done — tag `test-dashboard-v*`). But the rule text doesn't mention `dashboards/**`.

Seraphine used `feat:` on #152 (semantically correct). Jayce/Vi/Ekko used `chore:` out of caution. Pre-push hook behavior on this path is unknown.

Pick one:
- **(a) `feat:` correct** — amend rule 5 to list `dashboards/**` alongside `apps/**`. Check hook includes the path.
- **(b) `chore:` correct for now** — dashboards/ isn't under release-please yet until A2's config actually runs. Have Seraphine change #152 to `chore:`.

Without an answer, either Jhin flags #152 for prefix change (noise) or the merge wave lands inconsistent prefixes.

---

**3. Merge batching: solo or wait for more green?**

#149 Ekko is dual-green right now (Jhin + Azir both LGTM). Four more will likely go dual-green in the next cycle (#146, #147, #150, #148 once Azir's ADR patch lands).

Pick one:
- **(a) Merge #149 now** — unblocks TDD hooks on main immediately; every future PR then CI-gated correctly. Caveat: Vi's #146 will have a trivial conflict to resolve (template was her file) but she's already stripped her diff, so clean merge.
- **(b) Wait for batch of 4–5 dual-greens** — one merge pass, less churn, but delays Ekko's hooks becoming authoritative.

Recommendation: **(a)**. Merging #149 first makes the hooks live, so every subsequent PR gets TDD-gated on the real hook. Small churn for big gain.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-18T07:15:16Z

Step-by-step for F4. Do this locally on your machine (not an agent — rule 6).

**1. Generate the INGEST_TOKEN**
```bash
openssl rand -hex 32
```
Copy the hex string.

**2. Write two plaintext env files to a tmp location (NOT inside the repo)**
```bash
cat > /tmp/dashboards.prod.env <<EOF
INGEST_TOKEN=<the hex you just generated>
FIREBASE_PROJECT_ID=myapps-b31ea
GCS_BUCKET=strawberry-test-artifacts-prod
ALLOWED_UIDS=0DJzc86i5MP74jAwwT4YjvbcAub2,<Haruka's UID>
EOF
```
Same for staging (use `myapps-b31ea-staging` + `strawberry-test-artifacts-staging`).

**3. Encrypt with age to the repo recipient**
```bash
age -r age16zn6u722syny7sywep0x4pjlqudfm6w70w492wmqa69zw2mqwujsqnxvwm \
    -o secrets/encrypted/dashboards.prod.env.age \
    /tmp/dashboards.prod.env

age -r age16zn6u722syny7sywep0x4pjlqudfm6w70w492wmqa69zw2mqwujsqnxvwm \
    -o secrets/encrypted/dashboards.staging.env.age \
    /tmp/dashboards.staging.env
```

**4. Delete plaintext immediately**
```bash
rm /tmp/dashboards.prod.env /tmp/dashboards.staging.env
```

**5. Commit + push**
```bash
git add secrets/encrypted/dashboards.prod.env.age secrets/encrypted/dashboards.staging.env.age
git commit -m "ops: add encrypted env bundles for test-dashboard (F4)"
git push origin main
```

**Two things I need to confirm before you run this** (let Yuumi check) — the exact path `secrets/encrypted/dashboards.*.env.age` vs some other naming, and whether the plan wants a single bundle or per-env. Want me to have Yuumi verify, or just eyeball it?

Also: **what's Haruka's Firebase UID?** Only you have it. Grab it from Firebase Console → Authentication → Users.

</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="caitlyn" color="blue" summary="Staging hygiene: no git add -A in shared tree">
Third PR contamination issue caught by Azir (#150, #151, #152 all had unintended files swept in from other agents' in-flight memory/learnings). Cease-and-desist on `git add -A` / `git add .` in this working tree.

**Rule — applies to every agent, every commit:**

1. **Never** `git add -A` or `git add .`. Ever. Even if "your" change is trivial.
2. **Always** stage explicit files by path: `git add path/to/file1 path/to/file2`.
3. **Before every commit**, run:
   ```
   git status
   git diff --staged --stat
   ```
   Verify only YOUR intended files are staged. If you see anyone else's `agents/<name>/learnings/*.md` or `agents/<name>/memory/*.md` files, you've swept them in — unstage (`git restore --staged <path>`) and re-stage cleanly.

**Why it keeps happening:** strawberry is a shared working tree. Every agent's session writes to `agents/<their-name>/memory/` and `agents/<their-name>/learnings/` concurrently. If you're mid-task and another agent is writing learnings in parallel, their untracked files appear in your `git status`. `git add -A` picks them up silently. By the time Jhin reviews, your PR has files you've never heard of.

**Expected state of other agents' directories:**
- `agents/<other-agent>/memory/MEMORY.md` — may be modified by them while you work; leave it alone.
- `agents/<other-agent>/learnings/*.md` — may appear as untracked while they write; leave them alone.
- You only ever touch `agents/<your-own-name>/`.

**Applies equally to scripts and plan files.** Same mechanism, same fix: explicit-file staging.

In-flight branches that may already have contamination: #150, #151, #152 flagged by Azir. If your PR is open, run `git diff origin/main --stat` on your branch and confirm every listed file is intentional. If not, surgical `git restore --source=origin/main --staged <path>` then commit the fix.

Questions to me or Evelynn. This is my second broadcast of the day — please read.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="jhin" color="pink" summary="PR #153 F1+F2 reviewed — changes requested, two criticals">
PR #153 (F1+F2 auth) reviewed. Changes requested. Comment at https://github.com/Duongntd/strawberry/pull/153#issuecomment-4273103510

**CRITICAL #1 — timing side-channel reintroduced (F1):** `timingSafeEqual(tokenBuf, expectedBuf) || token !== expected` — the `|| token !== expected` is a variable-time string comparison that completely defeats the constant-time guarantee. An attacker measuring response times can still recover the token character by character. Fix: drop the `||` branch entirely; timingSafeEqual is the sole comparison. Also needs an explicit length check before padding — tokens longer than 64 bytes are silently truncated.

**CRITICAL #2 — rule 12 violated:** xfail commit (`f06cd17`) comes after the implementation commit (`003b6432`) on the branch. Rule 12 requires xfail-first. Branch history needs reordering.

**IMPORTANT #1 — empty ALLOWED_UIDS fails open (F2):** `allowed.size > 0 && !allowed.has(uid)` means an unset or empty `ALLOWED_UIDS` silently accepts any valid Firebase ID token. Should fail closed when allowlist is empty.

**IMPORTANT #2 — firebase-admin version conflict:** this PR adds `^12.0.0`; B1 (PR #150) adds `^13.8.0` to the same file. Needs coordination with Jayce — `^13.8.0` should win.

Viktor dropped `roles/firebaseauth.admin` entirely — confirmed correct, `verifyIdToken()` needs no IAM role.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="azir" color="red" summary="PR #153 architecture review posted">
PR #153 (Viktor, F1+F2) — architecture review posted.

**Clean PR — no plan drift, no cross-agent files.** Best scope discipline of the past four. Worth acknowledging to Viktor.

**ADR §7 conformance — mostly PASS:**
- Ingest token: constant-time compare, 64-byte padding, not JWT — matches §7 service-auth model.
- Firebase auth: `verifyIdToken()` with ADC (no `cert("")` path), UID allowlist via env CSV, correct status codes — matches §7 human-principal model.
- PR body notes "no IAM role needed — I2 finding applied by design." Viktor independently arrived at the correct model, aligning with the pending §9 amend.

**ONE BLOCKER (empty-allowlist fail-open):**
```ts
if (allowed.size > 0 && !allowed.has(decoded.uid)) { ...403... }
```
If `ALLOWED_UIDS` is unset/empty, the guard is skipped and ANY valid Firebase token gains access. §7 says "UID allowlist of exactly one" — empty must deny, not bypass. Fail-closed is non-negotiable for an auth gate. Fix is one line: drop the `allowed.size > 0 &&`.

**Flag for Jhin (not blocking from my side):** the `|| token !== expected` fallback in ingest-token defeats constant-time on mismatch paths. Defensible as null-byte backstop but timing-leaks. Jhin's judgment call.

**Coordination:** Viktor used `it.failing` (correct, not `it.todo`) — but #151's vitest exclude still hides `*.xfail.test.ts`. Must coordinate removal of that exclude or these tests never run.

<teammate-message teammate_id="jhin" color="pink" summary="PR #154 B3 reviewed — changes requested, two importants">
PR #154 (B3 signed URLs) reviewed. Changes requested. Comment at https://github.com/Duongntd/strawberry/pull/154#issuecomment-4273109138

**IMPORTANT #1 — invalid ArtifactKind in xfail test:** Both `it.failing` tests pass `"output"` as the `kind` argument. `"output"` is not in `ArtifactKind` — `ext["output"]` is `undefined` at runtime, so `objectPath` returns `runs/.../output.undefined`. When tests flip to passing (with a mock), the path assertion would silently accept a malformed path. Fix: use a valid kind like `"screenshot"`.

**IMPORTANT #2 — `storage()` creates a new client per call:** `new Storage(...)` on every `createUploadUrl`/`createDownloadUrl` invocation initialises gRPC channels and an auth client each time. Should be a module-level singleton.

**Caitlyn's xfail-exclude concern resolved:** C1's `d2e1e23` removed the problematic `exclude` — the xfail file will be picked up correctly once C1 merges. No action needed on this PR.

V4 signing, 15min TTL, and xfail commit ordering all correct.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="azir" color="red" summary="PR #150 re-review (LGTM) + PR #154 review posted">
Both done.

**PR #150 re-review — cleared.** Confirmed both my original blockers are fixed at HEAD `7234702`:
- Scope: no more `plans/**` drift; eight files, all germane to B1.
- `cert("")` defect: now uses named-app ADC (`initializeApp({ projectId }, "dashboards-server")`) — matches Viktor's pattern in #153 and the correct Cloud Run approach. Bonus: named app avoids collision with the auth middleware's default app.
- Apologised to Jayce in the comment for not pulling fresh on the first pass.
- Architecture **LGTM**; waiting on Jhin.

**PR #154 (Jayce, B3 signed URLs) — ONE BLOCKER:** artifact path collision.

Current path: `runs/<runId>/<caseId>/<kind>.<ext>`. This means only one artifact per (case, kind) — second screenshot of the same case silently overwrites the first. ADR §3 declares `storage_path` as artifact-specific; §4 says callers declare by `local_ref` + kind; §5's example shows `screenshot-0.png` (indexed). E2E and QA flows routinely produce multiple screenshots per case — this breaks both silently.

Fix: add the artifact ID (or local_ref) to the path. Signature becomes `createUploadUrl(runId, caseId, artifactId, kind, mime)`, path becomes `runs/<runId>/<caseId>/<artifactId>-<kind>.<ext>`.

Otherwise: V4 ✓, 15-min expiry ✓, env-driven bucket with fail-closed ✓, upload contentType binding ✓. Also noted for D4 handoff that §5's `pinned/` prefix support would naturally live in this file as a helper.

Nine PRs reviewed. #150 architecture-cleared, #154 has one path fix pending.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="azir" color="red" summary="Wave 5: #159 LGTM, #165 LGTM, #169 two blockers">
Three new reviews posted:

**#159 (Viktor, I1 deploy) — LGTM.** Clean ADR §2a composition (two frontends into `public/{test,monitoring}/`), §7 public ingress with in-app auth, §9 audit log schema correct, idempotent via git-SHA tagging. Minor flag: uses `gcr.io` host (legacy GCR, Artifact Registry under the hood but deprecated host) — works now, needs migration before GCR shutdown. Non-blocker.

**#165 (Ekko, C2 pnpm wiring) — LGTM.** Minimal 9-line case-statement switch for `dashboards/*` paths. Plan §3 rule 3 is PM-agnostic so this is purely an invocation detail. xfail-first correctly seeded. `ops:` prefix right for a scripts-only change.

**#169 (Jayce, D1 reporter) — TWO BLOCKERS:**

1. **`artifact_uploads` missing from POST body.** ADR §4's ingestion contract requires declaring artifacts by `local_ref` + kind + size in the initial POST so the server returns signed upload URLs keyed by `local_ref`. This impl never emits `artifact_uploads` and the `cases[].artifacts` field is hardcoded `[]`. Works for Phase 1 unit+smoke (no artifacts), silently drops Playwright traces/videos/screenshots for E2E+QA. Either scope the PR explicitly to "unit+smoke only" in header comments, or implement the declaration now.

2. **`local_ref` treated as file path.** The upload loop does `artifact_file="${local_ref}"` and `[ -f "$artifact_file" ]`. Per ADR §4, `local_ref` is a *logical* name (e.g. `"screenshot_0"`) chosen by the caller; the caller maps it to an on-disk path. Script conflates the two. Fix requires the normaliser emit a separate `local_ref → path` mapping.

**Also a coordination note for Jhin** (flagged in the comment): normaliser generates `case_${Date.now()}_random` IDs client-side. ADR §3 specifies ULID IDs assigned server-side. If server trusts client IDs that's an injection/collision surface; if server overwrites, the client generation is just dead code. Needs Jhin's call.

Shape-wise D1 is correct — three-stage flow (POST → PUT → finalize), §13 per-type behaviours (unit 2s fire-and-forget, e2e soft-fail, others hard-fail), §3 run schema. Good foundation once the contract gaps close.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="azir" color="red">
{"type":"idle_notification","from":"azir","timestamp":"2026-04-18T07:32:19.283Z","idleReason":"available"}
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="caitlyn" color="blue" summary="C2 duplicate — #161 vs #165 conflict">
**Duplicate C2 implementations — need your call on which wins.**

- **PR #161** (branch `chore/c2-dashboards-hook-wiring`, author "ekko" per earlier message). Claims the existing `pre-commit-unit-tests.sh` from #149 is already generic and picks up any `tdd.enabled:true` package. Scope: **test-hooks.sh only** — adds 20/20 verification coverage. No change to the hook itself.

- **PR #165** (branch `chore/c2-precommit-dashboards`, author "ekko-c2" per just-now message). Claims the hook needed an explicit case branch — staged files under `dashboards/*` now run `pnpm -C "$pkg" test:unit`, other TDD-enabled packages keep `npm run test:unit --if-present`. Scope: **pre-commit-unit-tests.sh AND test-hooks.sh** — real hook modification + xfail-first discipline (xfail SHA → impl SHA).

These are substantively incompatible claims about whether the hook needs pnpm-vs-npm wiring for dashboards packages. One of them is wrong.

**Possibility analysis:**
1. **#161 is right** — the hook from #149 uses `--if-present` which gracefully handles pnpm workspaces, and dashboards/ picks up automatically. #165 added unnecessary pnpm special-casing.
2. **#165 is right** — the hook from #149 runs `npm run test:unit` which fails (or silently no-ops) for pnpm-workspace packages, so dashboards/ test:unit actually wasn't running without the explicit case branch. #161's "20/20 verification" may have been testing a different code path than the one broken.
3. **Both partly right** — #161 is right that the hook detects `tdd.enabled:true` packages generically, but wrong that it executes their test scripts correctly without pnpm wiring. #165 is the fix #161 missed.

I lean (3) — a pnpm workspace invoked via `npm run test:unit` from a hook's `cd $pkg && npm run ...` pattern would either fail or no-op. #165's `pnpm -C "$pkg" test:unit` is the correct invocation. #161's verification tests may have inadvertently exercised a codepath that happened to work (e.g. if the tests ran on a package with a non-pnpm fallback).

**Recommendation:**
- Duong verifies which actually runs tests by making a staged change under `dashboards/server/src/**` and committing — does the hook run `pnpm -C dashboards/server test:unit` and show output? If yes, #161 was sufficient. If no (silent no-op or error), #165 is the real fix.
- If #165 is correct: close #161, merge #165. The "ekko-c2" session found a real gap the first session missed.

## Duong — 2026-04-18T07:35:24Z

<teammate-message teammate_id="caitlyn" color="blue" summary="CRITICAL: it.failing is not valid Vitest — use it.fails">
Third critical silent-defeat defect in the TDD pipeline, caught by Vi. Broadcast to prevent further spread.

**Wrong:** `it.failing("xfail: ...", () => { ... })`
**Right:** `it.fails("xfail: ...", () => { ... })`

**Why it matters:** Vitest 4.x exports `it.fails`, NOT `it.failing`. `it.failing` is Playwright's API. When Vitest hits `it.failing(...)` it throws `TypeError: it.failing is not a function`, the test file fails to parse, and **zero tests register**. The file appears to "pass" (nothing ran = nothing failed) — same silent-no-op pattern as the Vitest exclude-glob defect from #151.

The Pyke `tdd-workflow-rules.md` plan text referenced `it.failing` generically. That wording was written plan-agnostic of specific frameworks but has led everyone seeding xfails to copy-paste the wrong Vitest API.

**Action items per in-flight branch:**

| PR/branch | Files affected | Fix owner |
|---|---|---|
| #154 B3 signed-urls | `signed-urls.xfail.test.ts` | Vi (pushing fix) |
| #153 F1+F2 | `ingest-token.xfail.test.ts`, `firebase.xfail.test.ts` | Vi (pushing fix) |
| #152 G1 | `App.xfail.test.tsx` | Vi (pushing fix) |
| future F3 CORS | `cors.xfail.test.ts` | Vi (when seeded) |
| Any other Vitest xfail | anywhere | author must use `it.fails` |

**Ekko action item:** `tdd-gate.yml` hook grep pattern currently matches `it.failing`. Please update it to ALSO match `it.fails` (the canonical Vitest form). Both strings should be recognized as TDD-disciplined xfail markers — `it.failing` stays valid for Playwright E2E tests; `it.fails` for Vitest unit tests.

**Evelynn action item (flagged separately):** The Pyke tdd-workflow-rules plan text needs a §2 Definitions amendment to spell out the per-framework canonical API explicitly: Vitest = `it.fails`, Playwright = `test.fail`, pytest = `@pytest.mark.xfail`. Prevents the next session from making the same mistake I did in my cluster brief to Vi.

**Verification step for every future xfail commit:** run `pnpm -C <pkg> test:unit` locally, confirm the xfail FILE appears in the test count with status "failing as expected" (or equivalent). If the test count doesn't include it, the file is silently unparsed — fix the API and re-verify before committing.

Vi just landed #170 as the canonical example of the corrected pattern (health.xfail flip + firestore-rules fix). Use it as a template.

This is the third of three silent-defeat defects this workstream has surfaced (exclude-glob, `git add -A` contamination, wrong xfail API). The common theme: TDD rules that fail silently rather than loudly are the worst kind of rules. Everyone's already doing the right thing by reading diffs and running tests before commit — keep it up.
</teammate-message>

**The defect:** `it.failing` is Playwright's API. Vitest 4.x uses `it.fails`. Any Vitest test file using `it.failing(...)` throws `TypeError`, fails to parse, registers ZERO tests, and silently passes. Same class as the exclude-glob defect from #151.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-18T07:35:38Z

**CI failures — explained.** Caitlyn's team just caught a hidden defect: **`it.failing` is Playwright's API, not Vitest's — Vitest uses `it.fails`**. Every xfail test file that used `it.failing(...)` throws `TypeError` at parse time, registers zero tests, and silently passes. The CI checks that _should_ have been green are actually failing because the xfail files don't parse.

This affects #152, #153, #154, and maybe others. Vi is pushing fixes (#170 has the canonical corrected pattern). Once fixes propagate, CI should clear.

**So:** the current failures are **real, but expected during this fix cycle**. Don't merge anything with `it.failing` in a Vitest test file until it's patched.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-18T07:37:16Z

Good news: **the rule already exists.**
- **Rule 15** — "PRs cannot merge red."
- **Rule 18** — "no red required check, no `--admin` bypass."

The reason it hasn't been stopping you is **branch protection on main doesn't have required status checks configured** — the rule is text-level, not enforcement-level. And your account has bypass permissions (which is why only agents are blocked today, not you).

**To make it actually block merges in GitHub UI:**
1. Configure branch protection on `main` with required status checks: `Lint + Test + Build (affected)`, `TDD Gate`, `validate-scope`, `QA report present`, etc.
2. Keep your bypass privilege (break-glass) but set the checks as required for non-bypass accounts — you'll still see the red warning, and the merge button gets a confirmation prompt.

**OR go stricter:** include yourself in the no-bypass policy. Merge button literally disabled until all checks green. You lose break-glass but gain guaranteed safety.

Want me to dispatch Camille (git/security advisor) to write the branch protection config + Ekko to execute? Quick to do.

<teammate-message teammate_id="vi" color="purple" summary="it.failing vs it.fails — details">
`it.failing` is a Playwright API that doesn't exist in Vitest — calling it throws `TypeError: it.failing is not a function` and the entire test suite crashes (exit non-zero), which breaks CI. `it.fails` is the correct Vitest 4.x API; semantics are identical: the test is expected to throw/fail, and Vitest records it as a pass if it does. The distinction matters because a crashed suite looks like a test failure to tdd-gate.yml, not an expected-fail. Affected branches confirmed: `chore/b3-signed-urls` (fixed and pushed this session). The F1/F2 branch (`chore/f1-f2-f4-auth`) already used `test.fails` correctly. All other xfail files I seeded this session used `it.fails` from the start. A sweep is not needed — the cluster is clean. Suggest Ekko add a note to the pre-push hook or tdd-gate error output pointing to `it.fails` so future implementers don't hit this, but no emergency broadcast needed.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="vi" color="purple">
{"type":"idle_notification","from":"vi","timestamp":"2026-04-18T07:42:06.827Z","idleReason":"available"}

<teammate-message teammate_id="caitlyn" color="blue" summary="#161 wins empirically — #165 introduces a bug">
Ran the empirical check. **Your earlier ruling needs reversing: #161 wins, #165 should be closed.**

**Root cause of my earlier analysis error:** I assumed pnpm workspace because everyone was writing `pnpm -C ...` in scripts. **The project actually uses npm workspaces.** Root `package.json` declares:

```json
"workspaces": ["apps/portal", "apps/myapps", ..., "dashboards/*"],
"packageManager": "npm@11.7.0"
```

Not pnpm. The `pnpm -C dashboards/server test:unit` calls in various scripts happen to work because pnpm respects npm workspace config and the lockfile isn't committed, but the **canonical workspace manager is npm** per package.json.

**Implication for C2:**

- **#161 (Ekko verify-only) is correct.** The existing hook from #149 uses `(cd "$pkg" && npm run test:unit --if-present)` which is the correct invocation for this project's actual workspace manager. Ekko's first instinct — "the hook is already generic, no code change needed" — was right. His 20/20 verification tests were accurately exercising the real codepath.

- **#165 (Ekko-c2 pnpm wiring) is WRONG.** It hardcodes `pnpm -C "$pkg" test:unit` where the canonical invocation is `npm run test:unit`. Anyone without pnpm on their machine would have their pre-commit hook break. It's a latent defect, not a fix.

- **My earlier possibility (3) analysis was wrong**: I assumed `npm run test:unit` would silently no-op because "pnpm workspaces need explicit pnpm -C." Since this is an npm workspace, not pnpm, `npm run test:unit` from `cd dashboards/server` works exactly as intended once deps are installed (workspace-hoisted `vitest` binary in root `node_modules/.bin/`).

**Revised recommendation: close #165, merge #161.** Jhin's R23 LGTM on #161 was the accurate read; my framing that forced you to rule #165 wins was based on the wrong workspace-manager assumption. Apologies for the misdirection.

**One caveat worth knowing:** when the hook actually runs, it needs root `node_modules/` to be populated (via `npm install` at repo root). CI runs this. Local dev assumes developer has run `npm install` themselves. Neither is special — standard npm workspace behavior.

**Also noted: #177 D2 landed** — Phase 1 exit unblocker per your message. I'll ping Jhin + Azir for review right after this.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="azir" color="red" summary="PR #177 D2 — two real blockers">
PR #177 (Jayce, D2 POST /api/runs) — architecture review posted. **Two blockers**, both small fixes.

**The good:** this endpoint gets the §4 declare-then-upload contract RIGHT, unlike D1. It accepts `artifact_uploads[]` in the body, generates V4 signed URLs keyed by `local_ref`, returns `{run_id, artifact_upload_urls}`. Also server-assigns ULIDs per §3 (`run_${ulid()}`, `case_${ulid()}`, `artifact_${ulid()}`) — **this confirms D1's client-side ID generation is dead code**; D1 should strip it. Firestore batch transactionality, path-prefixed `/api/v1/`, proper §6 error shape, ingest token middleware all correct.

**BLOCKER 1 — `failure_stack` truncation missing.** ADR §3 requires "truncated to 8KB". Current code writes `c.failure_stack ?? null` verbatim. One-line fix: `c.failure_stack?.slice(0, 8192) ?? null`. This is the invariant I flagged to D2 in my B1 review; it wasn't carried through.

**BLOCKER 2 — Artifact docs never written.** `artifact_uploads` are accepted, signed URLs generated, URLs returned — but no `Artifact` Firestore doc is ever written, and `cases[].artifacts` is never backfilled with the server-generated artifact IDs. §3 declares Artifact as a first-class entity; without docs, declared artifacts are ghosts (signed URLs returned to client, zero server-side record, §5 pinning/lifecycle can't target them). Acceptable resolutions: (A) write Artifact docs in the same batch with status=pending, or (B) defer to D3 /finalize — but if B, the split MUST be explicitly declared in a comment so D3 inherits the contract.

**Flags (non-blocker):**
- No input validation beyond `type` — arbitrary strings accepted for `environment`, `status`, etc. Ingress-gated so constrained, but Zod-style validator would be hygienic as a follow-up.
- Bundled `auth/ingest-token.ts` and `storage/signed-urls.ts` from #153/#154. Needs sequencing: merge #153/#154 first (both have my arch LGTM), then #177 syncs main and deletes duplicates.

xfail discipline correct (seed at `dadcb4e` before flip at `85011e6`; test file uses real `describe/it`, not xfail markers — post-flip state is correct).

Ten architecture reviews this session. #177 is the Phase-1-exit gate — good shape, needs the two fixes.
</teammate-message>

## Evelynn — 2026-04-18T07:49:26Z

**GitHub Actions billing.** Yuumi's diagnosis of #153's 13 check failures found the literal GitHub error message attached to every failed job:

> "The job was not started because recent account payments have failed or your spending limit needs to be increased."

Means one of:
1. Monthly Actions minutes quota hit
2. Payment method on file failed (expired card, etc.)
3. Spending limit needs raising

**Check:** Go to https://github.com/Duongntd/strawberry/settings/actions or your org-level https://github.com/organizations/Duongntd/settings/billing → "Billing & plans" / "Plans and usage" → look for an alert banner or a red warning.

<teammate-message teammate_id="caitlyn" color="blue" summary="#177 forward-ports from #153/#154 — merge-order risk">
Worth flagging about #177 D2 (Jayce delivered it but I already had it queued for reviewers):

**Merge-order risk from forward-ports.** Jayce forward-ported two files into #177:
- `dashboards/server/src/auth/ingest-token.ts` ← from #153 (still in rework for it.failing fix)
- `dashboards/server/src/storage/signed-urls.ts` ← from #154 (still in rework for it.failing fix)

Both source PRs are not frozen. Three merge scenarios and risks:
1. **#177 first** → #153/#154 hit conflicts when they merge (redundant files now on main).
2. **#153/#154 first** → #177's forward-ports become silent duplicates that could drift from canonical.
3. **Batched together** → git auto-merge if diffs trivial; conflicts otherwise.

I asked Jayce to annotate the forward-ported files with a TODO comment pointing back to #153/#154 so Viktor/Jayce-b3 have a clear signal when they reconcile.

**Worth knowing for your batch-merge decision:**
- If you want maximum Phase-1-exit-velocity: batch-merge all three (#177 + #153 + #154) together; the git auto-merge will handle trivial line diffs, and post-merge a cleanup PR can dedupe.
- If you want lower risk: merge #153/#154 first (once their it.failing fixes land), then #177 rebases cleanly or has a small merge-main-in.
- Either way, D2 is Phase-1-exit critical. Not holding it indefinitely.

Not blocking; just informing. Duong's call when batch-merging.

1. Absolute-path `require()` anchored to `git rev-parse --show-toplevel` — fixes Jhin's R22 IMPORTANT properly.
2. **Subdirectory CWD regression test** in `scripts/hooks/test-hooks.sh` that asserts the hook correctly detects `tdd.enabled: true` when invoked from a subdirectory. `#161 doesn't have this test`.
3. Dropped fragile grep fallback — fail-hard on node-absent, per Jhin's suggestion.
4. **Removed `pnpm -C` wiring** — matches the npm-workspace reality we confirmed empirically.

**Net: #165 is no longer "wrong pnpm-vs-npm."** It's now converged to the correct npm-workspace posture PLUS adds a meaningful regression test #161 lacks. The original reversal rationale ("hardcodes pnpm where canonical is npm") no longer applies.

**Three options for you:**

**A. Stay with reversal, close #165.** Clean historical record (no "we changed our minds twice"). Subdirectory regression test is lost unless Ekko opens a tiny follow-up PR against merged #161 with just that test. Net ~30 min of extra work for the same end-state coverage.

**B. Keep both — merge #165 in addition to #161.** #161 is verify-only (no hook change). #165 is still-hook-change-but-correct-now. Merging both gives you: no-change verify from #161 + actual absolute-path fix from #165 + subdirectory regression test. Slight overlap in verification scope.

**C. Reverse again, close #161, merge #165.** "The fix version" becomes canonical. Undoes the reversal. Cleanest code state if you don't mind the yo-yo history. Risk: Ekko's R22 fix may introduce other subtleties not caught yet.

**My lean: (B).** #165's fix has landed cleanly and independently addresses a real gap (subdirectory-CWD) that #161 can't. Merging both is the least work for full coverage. The "overlap" is minor — #161's test-hooks.sh additions don't conflict with #165's, just extend them.

Billing *is* the blocker — Yuumi's original diagnosis was right; the only reason there's no red warning is that GitHub doesn't banner-alert when you silently hit the free cap.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-18T09:24:50Z

Yes, technically — but the trade-off math usually isn't worth it unless you expect steady monthly spend above ~$50.

**Option A — raise GitHub spending limit ($20/mo).** 15 seconds. Standard runners, zero maintenance.

**Option B — self-hosted runner on GCE.**
- Spin up an `e2-small` (not free; ~$12/mo) or reuse `bee-worker` (e2-micro free tier, but 1 vCPU + 1GB RAM will be slow for your CI).
- Install actions-runner, register to the repo, label as `self-hosted`.
- Change workflows: `runs-on: self-hosted` instead of `ubuntu-latest`.
- Harden: use ephemeral runners, restrict repo access, keep off prod VPC. Rule 16 QA Playwright jobs also need to run on this — Chromium in headless mode works fine on e2-small.
- Ongoing: security patches, runner upgrades, token rotation, flaky-job debugging (no standard pristine runner image).

**Risks specific to your setup:**
- Strawberry is a single-user repo but PRs could run arbitrary agent code — self-hosted runners executing PR workflows from a public fork is a supply-chain risk. For a private repo (yours) with only trusted pushers, lower risk.
- Duplicate infra with bee-worker (already running).

**My recommendation: raise the spending limit for now.** You're 13 days from reset anyway, and this workstream is in its final merge wave. If monthly Actions spend consistently >$30, revisit self-hosted — I'll have Heimerdinger write a proper migration plan then.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-18T09:24:56Z

Jhin idle.

## Duong — 2026-04-18T09:25:54Z

how about changing it to public?

## Evelynn — 2026-04-18T09:26:13Z

Technically yes — public repos get unlimited free Actions minutes. **But it's a very high-cost move for this repo specifically.**

What goes public:
- `agents/*/memory/*.md` — your personal context, work patterns, project notes, relationship details (Haruka references, work account details)
- `agents/*/learnings/*.md` — hundreds of files with project internals, mistakes, agent behavior
- `agents/memory/duong.md` — your profile
- `plans/**` — full architectural decisions, business logic, revenue intent for Dark Strawberry
- Full git history — scrubbed of literal secrets but contains all commit messages, review discussions, and any near-misses from before the secrets-guard hook was installed
- `secrets/encrypted/` is fine (age-encrypted), but anyone can try to brute-force it

It's also a one-way door — even deleting files doesn't remove them from git history without a `git filter-repo` + force push, and caches/forks preserve them anyway.

**Honest verdict: don't.** The $20/month spending limit is 10,000× cheaper than the time to audit and scrub this repo's history, and infinitely cheaper than leaking agent memory files.

If you want unlimited free CI long-term, **self-hosted runner on your e2-small is the right path** — not public. I stand by my earlier recommendation: raise the limit now, plan self-hosted migration if spend stays high after Phase 1 wraps.

**The stale-view phenomenon isn't just Jhin — Azir just hit it too on #180.**

Azir's updated R30 claims `--service-account` is missing per `gh pr diff 180 | grep service-account → no output`. But I just ran the same grep and got:

```
+  --service-account "dashboards-cloudrun@${PROJECT}.iam.gserviceaccount.com" \
```

And direct `git show origin/chore/i1-deploy-dashboards:scripts/deploy/dashboards.sh` line 100 has the line. Branch tip is `74e31ce` ("chore: attach dashboards-cloudrun SA to Cloud Run deploy").

**So this is cross-reviewer.** Both Jhin and Azir are seeing stale content for the same PR on the same day. That rules out "Jhin's local clone is broken" — this is a systemic issue on #180 specifically (or a pattern across today's PRs more broadly).

**Possible mechanisms (revised):**
1. **GitHub's PR diff endpoint is cached** for some window and reviewers are getting cached pre-`74e31ce` diff even when `gh pr diff` should pull fresh. Would be unusual but not impossible.
2. **Review-time context / inbox snapshots** capture PR state at a moment and reviewers re-render against that snapshot rather than live.
3. **Reviewer sessions have their own checkout** and the branch-fetch isn't updating.
4. **Something about the merge-main-in churn on #180** is confusing the diff display — two merge commits in the branch history may cause `gh pr diff` to sometimes show a stale baseline.

I've asked Azir to `git fetch origin chore/i1-deploy-dashboards && git show --stat` to confirm whether his local view matches `74e31ce`. If fetch-refresh resolves, mechanism (2) or (3). If his view persists showing pre-`74e31ce` content post-fetch, mechanism (1) or (4).

**Practical impact:** #180 is functionally ready to merge (gcr.io→AR, POSIX, unauth comment, SA attachment all present), but both reviewers are blocked on phantom findings. If you can direct-ping either of them from your end asking to refresh and re-verify with explicit `gh pr diff 180 | grep service-account`, that may shortcut the back-and-forth.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-18T09:28:07Z

Good strategic move — but **timing matters a lot.**

**Yes, this works long-term.** Split model:
- **Public repo** (`Duongntd/dashboards` or similar) — `apps/**`, `dashboards/**`, `.github/workflows/**`, `scripts/**`. Unlimited Actions. Gets community visibility for Dark Strawberry.
- **Private strawberry** — `agents/**`, `plans/**`, `assessments/**`, `architecture/**`, `secrets/encrypted/**`. Agent infra + design docs only.

**What you save:** $20–50/month in Actions, forever.
**What it costs:** migration work, history audit, workflow re-plumbing, GH secrets re-provisioning, branch protection re-config, team cutover.

**Migration risks to plan for:**
1. **History audit** — `git log -- apps/ dashboards/ scripts/` scanned for any past secret near-misses. Scrub with `git filter-repo` before publishing.
2. **Open PRs #146–#182 would all be orphaned** — they'd need to be closed in strawberry and re-opened in new repo, OR merged first in strawberry and migration happens against clean main.
3. **Agent memory references** — `agents/*/memory/*.md` and `plans/**` have commit SHAs baked in. Those SHAs point to strawberry; if you rewrite history in the new repo, they drift.
4. **CI wiring** — Firebase service accounts, Google Cloud SA keys (GH secrets `GCP_SA_KEY_PROD/STAGING`, `AGE_KEY`, `BEE_SISTER_UIDS`) re-provisioned in new repo.
5. **Branch protection + TDD hook scripts** — move to new repo.
6. **Cross-repo PR UX** — agent work spans both repos. Plan in strawberry, code PR in public repo. More friction for you as the merger.

**My strong recommendation: do this AFTER Phase 1 exit, not now.**

- Right now 10 PRs are in flight. Migration mid-flight = 10× churn.
- Raise the $20 budget to finish Phase 1 (cost you probably <$5 before reset).
- Have Azir write a `plans/proposed/2026-04-19-public-app-repo-migration.md` plan post-Phase-1.
- Clean cutover window: merge everything, scrub history, split, switch agent workflows.

Want me to have Azir draft the migration plan in background while we finish Phase 1, so it's ready for execution immediately after?

## Evelynn — 2026-04-18T09:45:57Z

Want to check what you mean — two readings:

**A) Switch your Strawberry coordination session to Windows** (Windows Mode exists per memory — `windows-mode\launch-evelynn.bat`). Continuity preserved through shared repo files. Doesn't help CI.

**B) Use the Windows box as a self-hosted GitHub Actions runner** to get free unlimited CI.

For (B), honest assessment: **not a great fit for this workstream.** The workflows are POSIX-shaped — bash scripts, `age` encryption, git hooks, `npm` invocations from Unix paths. Running on native Windows breaks line endings, shell semantics, and path conventions. You'd need WSL2 + Docker to make it viable, which is another setup project.

GCE e2-small at ~$12/mo is the cleaner self-hosted path if you want to avoid GitHub Actions billing long-term.

**For right now though, $20 one-time spending limit raise to unblock Phase 1 exit is still the shortest path.** Windows runner setup would be a couple hours minimum before CI clears.

Which did you mean — A or B?

## Duong — 2026-04-18T09:47:22Z

<teammate-message teammate_id="caitlyn" color="blue" summary="#182 merge as-is at a5f9fde; new hook-logic gap discovered">
Viktor diagnosed the #182 push-block: **pre-push TDD hook has a logic gap.** It scans only the push delta for xfail-first discipline, not branch history. So a rename-only follow-up commit pushed AFTER the xfail commit has already landed on origin gets falsely flagged as "xfail-less implementation."

Viktor's `2cb1c82` on `chore/f3-cors-middleware` is exactly that case:
- `1af8737` xfail commit (already on origin)
- `816edb3` impl commit (already on origin)
- `2cb1c82` rename-only cosmetic commit (blocked by hook because push delta = just `2cb1c82`, which touches `dashboards/server` src with no xfail in the delta)

**Recommendation to you (and by extension Duong): merge #182 as-is at `a5f9fde`.** Rename + `UI_ALLOWED_METHODS` removal land as a trivial post-merge chore PR. Both reviewers' LGTMs cover `a5f9fde` content.

**Adding to governance list:**
6. `pre-push-tdd.sh` scan should walk branch history (base..head), not just push delta. Current logic false-positives on post-xfail-landed cosmetic commits. Worth a small Ekko follow-up PR. ## Duong — 2026-04-18T09:49:08Z

<teammate-message teammate_id="caitlyn" color="blue" summary="Azir extends #180 LGTM + adopts "extend-absent-arch-changes" rule">
Azir extended his #180 LGTM to current tip `1b4673b` (pnpm→npm is trivial, no arch delta). **All 11 PRs in the merge-ready pool now unambiguously dual-green.**

**More importantly — Azir adopted as a standing rule:**

> "Architecture LGTM extends to future tips of the same PR absent architectural changes. ADR-surface concerns (route semantics, auth model, data model, IAM, deploy topology, API contract) warrant explicit re-review; everything else the prior LGTM carries."

This is a meaningful process improvement worth capturing beyond this session:
- Reduces the rescan-on-every-trivial-push friction we've been burning cycles on
- Matches Jhin's operating mode (he re-reviews explicitly when substantively new findings, accepts via "LGTM stands" when fix maps to prior review)
- Formalizes what's effectively the default in most review cultures

Worth considering for `architecture/review-policy.md` or equivalent doc as a team-level norm. Or just capture it in the reviewer-agent system prompts so both Jhin and Azir's future sessions carry the same rule.

Everything else — **merge pool is clean, 11 PRs ready, Duong's call to batch-merge.**

Adding to the governance list:
4. Extend-LGTM-absent-arch-changes rule worth formalizing as workstream policy

<teammate-message teammate_id="camille" color="blue" summary="blocker: invariant #18 two-reviewer rule vs single-account reality">
Blocker on merging B10 PRs (and by extension every other dep PR today). Invariant #18 requires "one approving review from an account other than the PR author."

Reality: ekko and I are both posting reviews under the same GitHub identity `harukainguyen1411`. Ran `gh pr view 107 --json reviews` and both her approval and mine show identical author.login. So from GitHub's perspective there's one reviewer (non-dependabot), not two.

Technical interpretation:
  - Letter of invariant #18: "one approving review from an account other than the PR author" — satisfied (one non-author account approved). → OK to merge.
  - Spirit (two-reviewer eyes): not satisfied — one human identity is rubber-stamping their own agent team's work.

I don't want to auto-merge on the letter if you wanted the spirit. Three options:
  (a) Accept letter-only interpretation for today's dep cleanup (given each PR is audited in-detail by ekko *and* re-reviewed by me, so there are two independent AI reviews even though one account); proceed to merge all B10 + future dep PRs with single-account approvals.
  (b) Rope in a human reviewer (Duong) for each merge — slower but spirit-compliant.
  (c) Create a second GitHub account for agent reviews so they show up as distinct identities — out of scope for today, plan-worthy.

I lean (a) for today's workstream given the scope (Dependabot bumps, not product code) and the two-AI-audit trail in the PR bodies. Your call.

All four B10 PRs are approved and CI-green/required-checks-satisfied; merges staged pending your decision.

Followup data point on the invariant #18 question.

Tried to approve ekko's PR #156 (B14 dependabot.yml config) and GitHub returned:
  `failed to create review: GraphQL: Review Can not approve your own pull request (addPullRequestReview)`

GitHub is enforcing author!=reviewer at the identity level. Since ekko and I are both `harukainguyen1411`, GitHub sees me as the author of her PR and refuses.

Implications:
- **Dependabot-authored PRs** (B10 #107/#55/#54/#106, B4g #155) — author is `dependabot[bot]`; ekko and I can still technically cross-review (though we both show as the same account, neither is the author, so approvals post). That's where the "letter vs spirit" question lives.
- **Agent-authored PRs** (B14 #156, all upcoming B11/B11a/B11b/B12/B13 PRs ekko will author) — GitHub outright blocks the second reviewer. There is no valid second reviewer under our current account setup.

Options shrink:
  (a') Accept letter-only for dependabot-authored PRs AND accept single-reviewer-only for agent-authored PRs (de facto bypass of #18's second-reviewer requirement). Weakest posture.
  (b) Duong as second reviewer on agent-authored PRs. Mandatory for today if we want any agent-authored merges to land.
  (c) Second GitHub account for agent reviews — the only structural fix; can't happen today.

Current stage:
  - B10 4 PRs: both reviews posted (shown as same account). Letter-compliant; spirit-at-risk. Awaits your call (a).
  - B14 #156: my review couldn't post. Blocked structurally; needs you or Duong.

Your call.

## Duong — 2026-04-18T06:20:56Z

ok good. how can we improve this in the future? Like if I have 3 stream with you, you should remember all 3

## Evelynn — 2026-04-18T06:21:20Z

Root cause: my memory is a single file (`agents/evelynn/memory/evelynn.md`), and when three sessions close in parallel they race/overwrite. Only one stream's summary survived into memory — the other two left journal entries and learnings but no top-level session note. So when I booted today, I only saw S44.

Three ways to fix this, cheapest to most robust:

**1. Append-not-overwrite protocol (lightest)**
Modify `/end-session` so when it writes the "Sessions" bullet in `evelynn.md`, it *appends* a new entry per session-ID instead of replacing the last one. Each parallel session gets its own line. Safe against races if we do it as an atomic append (single line), but still fragile if two write in the same second.

**2. Per-session shards + merge on startup (medium)**
Each session writes to `agents/evelynn/memory/sessions/<session-id>.md` at close. At startup, I read the shards newer than last consolidation and fold them into `evelynn.md`. No races — each session owns its own file. Adds a consolidation step.

**3. Stream-aware sessions (most robust)**
When you launch parallel Evelynns, the first message declares the stream — "stream: deployment pipeline" / "stream: testing" / "stream: dependabot". Each session writes to a stream-scoped slot (`memory/streams/deployment.md`, `testing.md`, `dependabot.md`). Memory stays separate and Duong explicitly sees which stream is which. Combined with #2, this gives clean isolation AND consolidation.

I'd go **#2 + #3 combined**:
- You declare the stream when you open the session (or my startup hook asks if multiple are running)
- Each session writes to `memory/sessions/<session-id>.md` at close
- Next full session boot consolidates into `evelynn.md`, grouped by stream
- `last-session.md` becomes `last-sessions/` (one file per stream), so I load *all* recent handoffs

Want me to write this up as a proper plan? Azir or I can draft it — this is architectural enough that it deserves an approved plan before Jayce/Viktor touches the skill.

## Duong — 2026-04-18T06:23:08Z

ok I think 2 + 3 is good. Ask Lux, if she's ok then we do it

## Evelynn — 2026-04-18T06:23:29Z

Lux is reviewing. I'll relay her verdict when she comes back.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-18T06:24:03Z

Lux greenlights **Part A only, drop Part B**. Her reasoning is sharp:

**Why drop streams?** The race is the bug, not the lack of labels. Auto-sharding on session UUID (which already exists) is collision-free and requires zero UX from you. Stream labels drift silently ("testing" vs "tests" fragments memory forever).

**What she wants instead:**
1. `/end-session` writes shard → `agents/evelynn/memory/sessions/<uuid>.md` (uuid from the transcript already generated in the skill — free reuse)
2. `evelynn.md` becomes a **read-time view**, not a write target — either glob last N shards at startup, or consolidate at *session start* (single-writer: the booting session), archiving older shards
3. Same for `last-session.md` → `last-sessions/<uuid>.md`, SessionStart reads the whole directory (last ~5)
4. **Never consolidate at close** (race). **Never delete during consolidation** — move to `sessions/archive/`.
5. **Audit `remember:remember`** — same single-file race. Either shard it or treat `last-sessions/` as authoritative.

She also flagged a minor inconsistency in `/end-session` skill metadata (line 4 says `disable-model-invocation: false` but docstring says true) — worth fixing while we're in there.

Good call on the counter-proposal. Want me to commission Azir to write the architecture plan? Scope: shard-on-close, consolidate-on-boot, SessionStart reads the directory, audit remember plugin.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-18T06:28:49Z

Plan is live: `plans/proposed/2026-04-18-evelynn-memory-sharding.md` (commit `1aeee73`). Key decisions:

- **Shards** on close → `memory/sessions/<uuid>.md` + `last-sessions/<uuid>.md` (reuses transcript UUID, zero race)
- **Consolidation** via new `scripts/evelynn-memory-consolidate.sh` at fresh-session boot — flock-guarded, folds >24h shards under a `<!-- sessions:auto-below -->` sentinel in `evelynn.md`, archives originals, never deletes
- **`remember:remember` bypassed** for Evelynn (single-file race). Sonnet subagents keep it (one-shot, no race).

## Duong — 2026-04-18T06:30:17Z

1. 30 days
2. all within 48h

## Evelynn — 2026-04-18T06:30:30Z

On #3 — it's the same race we're fixing.

The `remember:remember` plugin writes to a single shared file (`.remember/remember.md`). When three parallel Evelynns close, they all write to that one file → last-writer-wins, two get overwritten. Exact same bug we're solving with shards.

Two options:
- **(A) Shard it too** — rebuild the plugin's write path to use per-session files. Bigger scope, touches an external plugin's contract.
- **(B) Bypass for Evelynn** — Evelynn just doesn't use `remember`, since our own shard system covers her memory. Sonnet subagents *keep* using it because they're one-shot (single agent per task, no race possible).

Lux picked B as the pragmatic path. It keeps the plugin useful everywhere it's safe and avoids forking external code.

Want B, or should we invest in sharding the plugin (A) so nothing gets left out?

## Evelynn — 2026-04-18T06:42:36Z

Jhin posted, and it's not clean. Two blockers + three important issues on PR #144:

**🔴 Blockers**
- **C1:** `trap ... EXIT` registered *after* the subshell lock. Early `pipefail` abort can release the lock file before the critical section finishes → concurrent boot double-rewrites `evelynn.md`. Fix: register trap before lock branch.
- **C2:** `git add -A` on the memory directory stages *anything* concurrent sessions might have written there (including temp/decrypted files). Gitleaks is a backstop, not a guarantee. Fix: stage only files the script explicitly touched.

**🟡 Important**
- **I1:** Archive prune uses post-`git mv` mtime — shards near the 30-day boundary get an extra 30 days.
- **I2:** UUID collision fallback only handles one collision. Second collision = `git mv` fails mid-loop with partial state.
- **I3:** `last-sessions/*.md` never pruned — accumulates in git forever.

Jhin's verdict: C1 and C2 are blockers; I1–I3 should be fixed in this PR, not a follow-up.

Waiting on Lux's take before I send Viktor back for rework.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-18T06:43:32Z

Lux confirmed the advisory principles landed cleanly, but finds the same trap bug from a different angle — Viktor's script sets a lock-cleanup trap on L42 then silently *overrides* it with a tempfile trap on L110 (bash only keeps the last trap per signal). On macOS noclobber path (production, since flock isn't installed) the lock file never gets cleaned → stale lock → every subsequent boot exits 0 as no-op. **That's worse than Jhin's read:** not just a race, but an outright wedge after one crash.

Consolidated blockers for Viktor to fix:

**🔴 Must-fix before merge**
1. **Trap handling** (Jhin C1 + Lux #2) — merge lock cleanup + tempfile cleanup into single EXIT trap, register *before* lock acquisition
2. **`git add -A` scope** (Jhin C2) — stage only explicit paths
3. **Archive prune mtime** (Jhin I1) — use shard content date, not post-`git mv` mtime
4. **UUID collision loop** (Jhin I2) — handle repeat collisions or fail loud with rollback
5. **`last-sessions/` prune** (Jhin I3) — match the 30d archive policy
6. **PID liveness check** on noclobber lock recovery (Lux #3)
7. **`command -v python3` guard** for Windows portability (Lux #4, Rule 10)

**🟢 Follow-up (separate issue, not blocking)**
- SessionStart hook should check consolidate exit code
- Persisted log file for consolidation failures
- Atomic `.tmp → mv` pattern in `/end-session` Step 7

Sending Viktor back in.

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry/.claude/skills/end-session

# /end-session — top-level session close

You are closing a top-level Claude Code session. This skill wraps the full close-session protocol into a deterministic checklist. Follow every step in order. Do not skip steps. Do not reorder.

## Argument

`` is the agent name whose session is being closed. If empty, default to `evelynn` (the top-level coordinator is the most common invocation). If `` is set to something other than a valid agent name (no matching `agents/<name>/` directory), refuse with `end-session: unknown agent <name>` and exit.

## Step 0 — Context probe

Run these Bash commands in a single call and keep the output in mind:

```
pwd
git status --short
git log -1 --oneline
date -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ
```

If the working tree has uncommitted changes unrelated to the session close (files outside `agents/<agent>/`, `scripts/`, `CLAUDE.md`, `.gitignore`), stop and report: `end-session: working tree dirty with unrelated files — commit or stash before closing`. Do not proceed.

## Step 1 — Discover source jsonl

Run the cleaner in dry-run mode (just discovery, no write) using the Bash tool:

```
python scripts/clean-jsonl.py --agent <agent> --session auto --out /tmp/end-session-probe.md
```

Note: for Phase 1, the cleaner does not have a separate dry-run flag. The `/tmp/` output path is a throwaway probe. After the probe, delete `/tmp/end-session-probe.md`.

Capture the stderr for any `CLEANER: chain ambiguous` warnings and relay them to the agent for confirmation before proceeding.

## Step 2 — Clean transcript

Run the cleaner for real:

```
python scripts/clean-jsonl.py --agent <agent> --session auto
```

The cleaner writes to the default path `agents/<agent>/transcripts/<YYYY-MM-DD>-<short-uuid>.md`.

- On exit code 0: record the output path from the cleaner's stdout.
- On exit code 1: report the error and stop. Do not proceed to any further step.
- On exit code 2: report the internal error and stop.
- On exit code 3: report the secret match verbatim, STOP IMMEDIATELY, do not stage any files, do not run the commit step. Escalate to Duong via the final report.

## Step 3 — Stage the transcript

```
git add agents/<agent>/transcripts/<YYYY-MM-DD>-<short-uuid>.md
```

Verify the file is staged with `git status --short`.

## Step 4 — (reserved for condenser, no-op in Phase 1)

Log `end-session: condenser step skipped — Phase 2 will wire Syndra's component A here` and continue.

## Step 5 — Journal append

Prompt the invoking agent (you, running this skill) to append their first-person reflection for this session to `agents/<agent>/journal/cli-<YYYY-MM-DD>.md`. Rules:

- Append only. Do NOT overwrite existing content.
- First-person voice. Not a transcript copy.
- 10–30 lines typical. No hard cap.

Use the Write tool if the file does not exist, Edit (append) if it does. After writing, stage the file:

```
git add agents/<agent>/journal/cli-<YYYY-MM-DD>.md
```

## Step 6 — Remember handoff

**If agent == evelynn:** Skip the `remember:remember` plugin entirely (it has a single-file race surface unsafe under concurrent close — see D6 in `plans/approved/2026-04-18-evelynn-memory-sharding.md`). Instead, write a new shard at `agents/evelynn/memory/last-sessions/<short-uuid>.md` where `<short-uuid>` is the UUID from Step 2's transcript path. Content: a structured 5–10 line handoff — date, session number, what happened, open threads, dangling commits or PRs, blockers. Stage:

```
git add agents/evelynn/memory/last-sessions/<short-uuid>.md
```

Note "remember:remember bypassed for evelynn — shard written to last-sessions/<short-uuid>.md" in the final report.

**If agent != evelynn:** Invoke the `remember:remember` skill via the Skill tool. This is the primary handoff mechanism — it writes `.remember/remember.md` with a structured snapshot of what is done, what is next, and any non-obvious context. The Remember plugin's `SessionStart` hook loads this automatically at the start of the next session.

```
Skill: remember:remember
```

Stage the output file:

```
git add .remember/remember.md
```

If the `remember` plugin is not installed or the skill is unavailable, fall back to writing `agents/<agent>/memory/last-session.md` manually with a 5–10 line terse handoff (date, what happened, open threads, dangling commits or PRs, blockers). Stage with `git add -f agents/<agent>/memory/last-session.md`. Note "remember step skipped — plugin not available, used last-session.md fallback" in the final report.

## Step 7 — Memory refresh

**If agent == evelynn:** Do NOT touch `agents/evelynn/memory/evelynn.md`. Instead, write a new shard at `agents/evelynn/memory/sessions/<short-uuid>.md` (same UUID from Step 2) containing:
- A `## Session YYYY-MM-DD (SN, <mode>)` heading.
- One-line summary of the session.
- Any delta notes to Key Context or Working Patterns that should be folded in at next consolidation.

Stage the shard:

```
git add agents/evelynn/memory/sessions/<short-uuid>.md
```

Note "evelynn memory shard written to sessions/<short-uuid>.md — consolidation will fold into evelynn.md at next boot" in the final report.

**If agent != evelynn:** Review `agents/<agent>/memory/<agent>.md`. If anything material changed this session (new working patterns, new known issues, sessions list), update it:

- Append a new session row to the `## Sessions` list with the format `- YYYY-MM-DD (SN, <mode>): <one-line summary>`.
- Prune stale entries if the file exceeds 50 lines. Remove the oldest session rows first.
- Update `## Key context` or `## Working patterns` only if the change is durable.

If nothing material changed, skip the update but still state "no memory changes this session" in the final report. Stage if modified:

```
git add agents/<agent>/memory/<agent>.md
```

## Step 8 — Learnings

If this session produced a generalizable lesson (something a future instance of this agent or a sibling agent would benefit from), write it to `agents/<agent>/learnings/<YYYY-MM-DD>-<topic>.md` and add a one-line reference to `agents/<agent>/learnings/index.md`.

If no learning, skip and state "no learnings this session" in the final report.

Stage any new learning files:

```
git add agents/<agent>/learnings/
```

## Step 9 — Commit + push

Build the commit message. Format:

```
chore: <agent> session closing — transcript, handoff, memory, learnings for YYYY-MM-DD <platform> session
```

Use `cli` as the platform for Claude Code sessions. Use HEREDOC form:

```
git commit -m "$(cat <<'EOF'
chore: <agent> session closing — transcript, handoff, memory, learnings for YYYY-MM-DD <platform> session

Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
EOF
)"
```

Then push:

```
git push
```

**If the pre-push hook rejects the commit** (wrong prefix, gitleaks hit, anything): STOP. Do not retry. Do not rewrite the commit. Report the error verbatim in the final report and exit with `end-session: commit rejected — manual intervention required`.

**If the push fails because main moved forward**: pull with merge (never rebase per CLAUDE.md git rules), then re-push. One retry only. If the second push fails, stop and report.

## Step 10 — Final report

Print a single-paragraph summary to the agent's output:

- Cleaned transcript path
- Commit hash
- Push status
- Journal / remember handoff / memory / learnings status (which were updated, which were skipped)
- Any warnings from the chain-walk or non-fatal errors along the way

Then exit. Do not close the session yourself — Duong or Evelynn explicitly ends the session after reviewing the report.

## Refusal posture

You are `disable-model-invocation: true`. The model cannot auto-fire you. Only explicit user invocation (`/end-session` in the CLI or Duong/Evelynn typing "run end-session") activates you. If any ambiguity about invocation, REFUSE with `end-session: requires explicit user invocation`.
